<div id="review_2209274802" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2209274802" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2209274802?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471176395" href="/book/show/39704614-what-if-it-s-us">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2209274802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8677793993956062557"><i>”This apartment isn’t home for either of us, but we’re home to each other, and that’s what makes every wall fall away so I only focus on him.”</i><br/><br/>When I heard that Becky Albertalli and Adam Silvera were writing a <s>love child</s> book together I instantly knew that I needed this in my life. XD Okay, it might have taken me a little while to get to it and I guess I kinda missed the hype train, but maybe this was good because I could focus on my own opinion instead of reading the opinion of others on my feed</span>
  <span id="freeText8677793993956062557" style="display:none"><i>”This apartment isn’t home for either of us, but we’re home to each other, and that’s what makes every wall fall away so I only focus on him.”</i><br /><br />When I heard that Becky Albertalli and Adam Silvera were writing a <s>love child</s> book together I instantly knew that I needed this in my life. XD Okay, it might have taken me a little while to get to it and I guess I kinda missed the hype train, but maybe this was good because I could focus on my own opinion instead of reading the opinion of others on my feed. ;-) <br /><br />And after finishing the final page let me tell you this: My opinion about this book is quite a strong one! *lol* I know there are a lot of people out there that ended up not liking <b>“What If It’s Us”</b> and I’m the first one to admit that it wasn’t exactly what I expected. If you’re looking for a fluffy and cute contemporary book you might be disappointed. Because yes, there is some fluff and cuteness going on but in this one it’s actually taking a backseat. At least it felt like that for me. <br /><br /><i>”But there were only so many hits to the heart I could take before I needed to step away. I gave him a lot of chances – I gave us a lot of chances. I just wasn’t good enough to remind him love could be a good thing.”</i> <br /><br />So what did Albertalli and Silvera try to achieve with this? If you ask me I think they wanted to write something realistic! And if they tried to do this, well, then they certainly nailed it! I mean at first I was a little bit disappointed about where this was heading too. I was hoping for a sweet romance and then I got Arthur and Ben! *lol* One of them some sort of innocent and naïve country bumpkin that only lives in the big city for the summer and the other a pretty disenchanted guy that is grumpy because his first love didn’t work out the way he hoped it would. <br /><br />I swear, I never read about a couple that would have been worse for each other than those two! *lol* And I’m meaning this in the best way possible. At first glance they have nothing in common and just don’t fit together, but as the story continued to unfold I realized that this was okay. They are two different people that don’t have a lot in common but despite their obstacles, their misunderstandings, their troubles and personal sensitivities they still work somehow.<br /><br /><i>”…, and our voices don’t ever really become one, but I like how we sound together.<br />Like two people trying to make it work.”</i><br /><br />I loved this quote because it’s so true! If you’re in a real relationship nothing is perfect. It’s easy to be in a relationship when you both still see things through rose-coloured glasses, but once this first stage of infatuation wears off a relationship is a lot of work. In Ben and Arthur’s case they just had to face those problems way earlier than others, they both tried to understand each other though and if you ask me I think this was a very mature approach. Speaking of which, another thing I really liked was the fact that both of them were already out of the closet. Ben’s entire family knew and Arthur told his people before he moved to New York. <br /><br /><i>”Yeah. I put up an Instagram post on Thanksgiving a couple years ago. Said that I was thankful for all the people in my life who are cool enough to love me as I am. And everyone else could unfriend me online and in real life. I had even checked my follower count before posting.”</i><br /><br />Gosh, how I wish everyone could be as brave as Ben! But then again, not everyone has a family and friends like him. Not all of us are fortunate enough not to be unfriended after a statement like that. No matter if it might be on Instagram or in real life. &gt;_&lt; Still, I liked that they were both comfortable with being who they truly are and it’s really rare to read an LGBTQ+ story in which the characters are already out. So kudos for that! Well, for that and for the amazing portrayal of realistic friendships! XD<br /><br /><i>Dylan claps. “Okay. I’m sold. I am shipping you with the boy you met when you were supposed to be shipping relationship relics to your last boy.”</i><br /><br />I loved Ben’s and Dylan’s friendship so much! They were amazing and their innuendos and jokes kinda reminded me of my bestie and me. *lol* I swear, when it comes to that we’re exactly like those two and it was so refreshing to see a friendship like ours represented on the pages of a book. Alone for that I couldn’t help but adore this story! I would never ever say anything like Ben to my bestie though. Phew! That was a really hurtful comment and I swear if my bestie would have said something like that to me I wouldn’t have talked to her either! I’m just glad Ben got his act together and apologized to Dylan in the end. XD<br /><br /><i>Samantha takes a step away from him. “A lightning bolt is going to burst in here any second now and shut you up.”<br />“I eat lightning for breakfast.”</i><br /><br />Samantha and Dylan were amazing too! &lt;3 They weren’t only made for each other and a truly perfect match, but also so damn funny that I couldn’t help but laugh out loud. ;-) Some people might say that Dylan was a little bit over the top, but let me tell you this: there are actually real Dylan’s out there in this world and if you’re very lucky one of them is a part of your life! XD<br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />At first I was a little bit disappointed because this went in an entirely different direction than I expected. The longer I read the more I got captivated by the story though. I began to appreciate it for its realistic and honest approach and with time all the characters and their individual flaws started to grow on me. If there is one thing I have to criticize then it’s <u>
  <b>THE ENDING</b>
</u>!!!! I mean OMG!!! To quote the Duke from Moulin Rouge: “I don’t like this ending!”<br /><u>WHY, Becky and Adam?!! WHY??!!!</u> I think I’ll never get over this ending and like so many others before me I demand a “do-over”! (See what I did there? *lol*) I’ll miss my two disaster gays so much and I’ll always want a sequel. #SorryNotSorry ;-P <br />This said: Happy Reading! <br /><br /><i>Arthur is tearing up. “Thanks for this. For everything. This morning. This summer. I know I’m a lot, and you’ve been so cool about it.”<br />I laugh a little. “We’re the worst. I mean, we’re the best. But we’re the worst. You always think you’re too much, and I feel like I’m not enough.”</i><br /><br />___________________________<br /><br />First reaction after the ending:<br /><br />OMG!! NUUUUU!!<br />Excuse me, WHAT?!<br />This can't be the ending! Like seriously! <br />Don't make fun of me!<br />The universe!!! THE FREAKING UNIVERSE APPROVED!!! <br />How is this ending even allowed? <br />Oh Boy, this is truly an Albertalli/Silvera book. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br />Full RTC soon! I need a shower with ice first! *lol*<br />__________________________________<br /><br />Pre-review:<br /><br />I’m in dire need of a fluffy m/m romance and since Becky Albertalli and Adam Silvera kinda rock this genre I decided to read <b>“What if it’s Us”</b>!<br /><br />Karma finding its way at a post office sounds like a good start, so I’m ready to be blown away. <br />Let’s hope the hype is real and those two managed to create something amazing! =)<br /><br />I loved <b>“Simon vs.”</b> and I only heard good things about Adam Silvera’s books so I think it’s about time to read one of them. ;-)<br /><br />To say it with the words of the Glee Cast: Hit it! *lol*</span>
  <a data-text-id="8677793993956062557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2213561966" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2213561966" />
    <a title="emi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34410191-emi"><img alt="emi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603747413p2/34410191.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2213561966?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emi" href="/user/show/34410191-emi">emi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=male-protagonist">male-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2213561966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8322732386022183644">Lately, when I read something I end up hating, I wonder if the problem is me and not the book. However, the problem was definitely the book this time.<br/><br/>All these four and five star ratings people are throwing at it? I don't understand. Did we read the same book? <br/><br/>I would talk about a plot, but there really wasn't a strong one. <br/><br/>I'd talk about the characters, but none of them were interesting enough to discuss.<br/><br/>And I'd talk about the chemistry, but the only chemistry in this book was the test that Ben</span>
  <span id="freeText8322732386022183644" style="display:none">Lately, when I read something I end up hating, I wonder if the problem is me and not the book. However, the problem was definitely the book this time.<br /><br />All these four and five star ratings people are throwing at it? I don't understand. Did we read the same book? <br /><br />I would talk about a plot, but there really wasn't a strong one. <br /><br />I'd talk about the characters, but none of them were interesting enough to discuss.<br /><br />And I'd talk about the chemistry, but the only chemistry in this book was the test that Ben probably should have failed. Wait did he fail? I honestly don't remember.<br /><br />About half this book was Hamilton references that could have been cut out completely. I love Hamilton just as much as the next guy, but Arthur has made me not want to listen to the soundtrack anytime soon. Plus mix in references to other musicals and Harry Potter on every other page. It was one, giant 400 page billboard. Especially to the company Lyft, which was mentioned no less than <br />5 times. <br /><br />Also, Ben's fantasy fanfiction of his life has obliterated all excitement I had for Adam Silvera's upcoming fantasy book. It was literally the least interesting book-inside-a-book ever.<br /><br />Also, speaking of fanfictions. This entire book felt like one. And not in a good way. I have all the respect for fanfictions, but fanfictiony writing is not for me. <br /><br />I think I'm just gonna avoid every Becky Albertalli book from now on. I don't have one nice thing to say about any of her last three books. But Adam, darling, I know you can do better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8322732386022183644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2374554089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15187465692973452977"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg' width='200' height='150' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Despite some very solid, and most importantly, age-appropriate, narrating from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6553678.Noah_Galvin' title='Noah Galvin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Noah Galvin</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18509789.Froy_Gutierrez' title='Froy Gutierrez' rel='nofollow noopener'>Froy Gutierrez</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36341204.What_If_It_s_Us' title='What If It's Us by Becky Albertalli' rel='nofollow noopener'>What If It's Us</a> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577278.Adam_Silvera' title='Adam Silvera' rel='nofollow noopener'>Adam Silvera</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7579036.Becky_Albertalli' title='Becky Albertalli' rel='nofollow noopener'>Becky Albertalli</a> fell <i>way</i> short of expectations. <br/><br/>I can <i>sort of</i> see why people like this love story (and yes, love story NOT ROMANCE), but I had <i>issues</i>.<br/><br/><b>There is no plot</b>. None. It is sort of a meandering, wandering story through the basically boring lives of two teenage boys. Lots of boring, boring stuff filling the page-time. Sure, there were amusing m</span>
  <span id="freeText15187465692973452977" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Despite some very solid, and most importantly, age-appropriate, narrating from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6553678.Noah_Galvin" title="Noah Galvin" rel="nofollow noopener">Noah Galvin</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18509789.Froy_Gutierrez" title="Froy Gutierrez" rel="nofollow noopener">Froy Gutierrez</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36341204.What_If_It_s_Us" title="What If It's Us by Becky Albertalli" rel="nofollow noopener">What If It's Us</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577278.Adam_Silvera" title="Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">Adam Silvera</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7579036.Becky_Albertalli" title="Becky Albertalli" rel="nofollow noopener">Becky Albertalli</a> fell <i>way</i> short of expectations. <br><br>I can <i>sort of</i> see why people like this love story (and yes, love story NOT ROMANCE), but I had <i>issues</i>.<br><br><b>There is no plot</b>. None. It is sort of a meandering, wandering story through the basically boring lives of two teenage boys. Lots of boring, boring stuff filling the page-time. Sure, there were amusing moments, but the cuteness, the humor, and the squee-factor wasn't there. <br><br><b>Romance lovers: this is not a romance. </b>A romance has a HEA and this just didn't. After all of that melodrama and discussion... just not satisfying. <br><br>I don't usually feel too old to read YA, but <b>but I felt old reading this</b>. It was full of silly drama that I just don't care about anymore, and I don't care to read it. <br><br>Despite some sweet moments and a decent narration, I wasn't in love with this audiobook. It took me nearly a month to finish, which is not a good thing. Disappointing. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time" rel="nofollow noopener">goodreads</a>|<a href="https://www.instagram.com/reading_all_night_long/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a>|<a href="https://twitter.com/DentistHeatherK" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>|<a href="http://www.myfictionnook.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a></span>

<div id="review_2787098913" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2787098913" />
    <a title="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52488949-lia"><img alt="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577875952p2/52488949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2787098913?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" class="user" itemprop="url" name="˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗" href="/user/show/52488949-lia">˗ˏˋliaˎˊ˗</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52488949-lia?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2787098913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5498364315196072888"><i> “i guess that’s any relationship. you start with nothing and maybe end with everything.” </i><br/><br/>this was probably my most anticipated book of the last year and all the more nervous i was because i had such high hopes and expectations. adam silvera and becky albertelli are two of my favorite authors and i loved all of their books (<i>leah on the offbeat</i> doesn’t exist). so, understandably, i wanted this to be great.<br/><br/>i loved that both of their writing styles mixed so well with one another and made this co-wr</span>
  <span id="freeText5498364315196072888" style="display:none"><i> “i guess that’s any relationship. you start with nothing and maybe end with everything.” </i><br /><br />this was probably my most anticipated book of the last year and all the more nervous i was because i had such high hopes and expectations. adam silvera and becky albertelli are two of my favorite authors and i loved all of their books (<i>leah on the offbeat</i> doesn’t exist). so, understandably, i wanted this to be great.<br /><br />i loved that both of their writing styles mixed so well with one another and made this co-written work seem so aligned. sure, at times you were able to distinguish distinct traits one or the author wrote, like when arthur was being super annoying and i couldn’t help but be reminded of leah and her annoying personality. however, it was great that both protagonists and their traits were depicted nicely based on each individual writing. especially reading about the characters’ development was interesting. they both each have their flaws but in the course of the story they come to change and grow and that contrast was absolutely beautiful.<br /><br />the story was surprisingly realistic! from the friendship dynamics to society’s expectations and problems they have to face in their daily lives, including jealousy and school. the scenes with their parents, especially in the beginning, were some of my favorites as you don’t really get to read that much about a character’s parents and families in books and they’re mostly just disregarded. this realism was taken to a point, however, that was pure exaggeration in my eyes. the amount of pop culture references at times prevented me to enjoy the story and left me really annoyed. look, i LOVE hamilton with my entire heart and all, but at some point it’s too much when it takes up what felt like a whole quarter of the book.<br /><br />from what i’ve seen, most people seem to quite hate the ending. i, on the other hand, absolutely loved it. it’s realistic and left me surprised because i didn’t expect the authors to take that step and just leave it at the good old cheese, so that was pleasant. all in all, <i>what if it’s us</i> is a beautiful story about two boys and their love story while having to face difficulties but who are still trying to make it work, or as arthur would say: <i>“i like disasters.”</i><br /><br /><b>
  <i>→ 4 stars</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5498364315196072888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2555718276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555718276" />
    <a title="☆ Todd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12415682-todd"><img alt="☆ Todd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539502816p2/12415682.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2555718276?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☆ Todd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☆ Todd" href="/user/show/12415682-todd">☆ Todd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2555718276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10321984270605412475"><br/><b>“<i>I guess that’s every relationship. You start with nothing and maybe end with everything.”</i><br/><br/>I LOVED-LOVED-LOVED this story so damn hard!<br/><br/>And I absolutely <i>HATED-HATED-HATED</i> how it ended!!!</b><br/><br/>The entire story was <b>compelling and full of humor</b>, which immediately hooked me and left me dying to find out what was going to happen next.<br/><br/><b>BUT...<br/><br/>The book ended with no HEA, not even an HFN.</b><br/><br/>Only a <b>"<i>what if</i>"</b>, where <b>*IF*</b> they end up living in the same city at the same time <b>*MAYBE*</b> they <b>*MIGHT*</b> pick up where they left </span>
  <span id="freeText10321984270605412475" style="display:none"><br /><b>“<i>I guess that’s every relationship. You start with nothing and maybe end with everything.”</i><br /><br />I LOVED-LOVED-LOVED this story so damn hard!<br /><br />And I absolutely <i>HATED-HATED-HATED</i> how it ended!!!</b><br /><br />The entire story was <b>compelling and full of humor</b>, which immediately hooked me and left me dying to find out what was going to happen next.<br /><br /><b>BUT...<br /><br />The book ended with no HEA, not even an HFN.</b><br /><br />Only a <b>"<i>what if</i>"</b>, where <b>*IF*</b> they end up living in the same city at the same time <b>*MAYBE*</b> they <b>*MIGHT*</b> pick up where they left off, instead of remaining forever in <b>The Friend Zone</b>.<br /><br />After going through everything they did (they had <b>FOUR "<i>first dates</i>" FFS!!!</b>) to finally become a "<i>we</i>", the romantic in me <b>hates that shit with the heat of 10,000 suns</b>.<br /><br />Yes, I understand when authors don't want to write the typical romance, but an epilogue with them <b>together</b>, finally, even 10 years down the road, that would've left me feeling as if this were a much more fulfilling story.<br /><br /><b>BUT (<i>again</i>)...</b><br /><br />Until Arthur left NYC, <b>never actually '<i>seeing</i>' Ben again</b> (<i>at least outside of FaceTime -- for over a YEAR, with zero plans to meet up again, UGH!</i>), the book was <b>nearly absolutely perfect</b>.<br /><br />Right from the beginning, <b>Arthur was completely blurty and adorable</b>, while <b>Ben was a bit more of a guarded, cool character</b>, and I loved them both immediately.<br /><br />Some of the lengths that Arthur went to to find his <b>Missed Connection</b> at the post office were bordering on stalker'ish, but nonetheless endearing. He was determined to get a second chance with the boy of his dreams, full stop.<br /><br />When they finally reconnected, though, their relationship wasn't immediate and effortless. They kept having repeated <b>do-overs of their first date</b>, but neither of them were ready to give up, because they *did* have a true connection. They just <b>needed to find their rhythm</b>, which they eventually did.<br /><br />The <b>drama with the side-characters</b> was a bit distracting, much like with Albertalli's "<i>Simon and the Homo Sapiens Agenda</i>", but I couldn't get enough of <b>Ben's girl-crazy, best friend, Dylan</b>, who reminded me an awful lot of <b>Stiles from Teen Wolf</b>. <blockquote>
  <b>Dylan calls me on FaceTime as I’m getting ready to meet up with Arthur.<br /><br /><i>“Hey,”</i> I say. I’m naked from the top up because I’m not sure which shirt I want to wear yet.<br /><br /><i>“Morning strip show,”</i> he says. “<i>Dylan like</i>.” </b>
</blockquote>Their close, usually-easy, nerdy friendship was a joy to read about and I wanted more.<br /><br />Both sets of <b>parents</b> were also great here, too, being completely supportive, going above and beyond the call of duty for their respective boys.<br /><br />So yeah, the book was <b>'<i>mostly</i>' great</b>, but I'm taking off a half-star due to the <b>truly disappointing lack of an HFN or HEA</b>, but also <b>BEGRUDGINGLY rounding up to 5 stars</b>, because <b>the rest of the book was just that good.<br /><br />-----------------------------------------------<br /><br />** Pro Tip:</b> <blockquote>If you aren't a huge musical theater fan, like I'm not, do yourself a huge favor in following the story and <b>watch the YouTube video of Ben Platt and Laura Dreyfuss perform ‘<i>Only Us</i>’ from ‘<i>Dear Evan Hansen</i>’ (below)</b> *before* getting too far into the story.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-FgEKPxcXEU&amp;t=182s">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-FgEK...</a></blockquote>-----------------------------------------------</span>
  <a data-text-id="10321984270605412475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2184025255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15236248491418957057"><b>What If It's Us ★ Most Anticipated 2018 </b><br/><i>Expected publication: October 2nd 2018 </i><br/><br/><u>
  <b>UPDATE: WHEN BECKY ALBERTALLI ACKNOWLEDGES YOUR FAN EDIT </b>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2627480340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17702080960819800987">I was smiling so hard that my cheeks hurt. And crying too. This could have been my favorite book of the year if I had gotten a walk into the sunset, but this ending had its own charm. Knowing anything can happen is more thrilling than a regular 'And then they lived happily ever after', right? <br/>And if there's anything Ben and Arthur are brilliant at, it's perfecting do-overs. So, fingers crossed!<br/><br/>I loved every single character to pieces but none more so than Arthur. <br/>Oh King Arturo!<br/>The very instant </span>
  <span id="freeText17702080960819800987" style="display:none">I was smiling so hard that my cheeks hurt. And crying too. This could have been my favorite book of the year if I had gotten a walk into the sunset, but this ending had its own charm. Knowing anything can happen is more thrilling than a regular 'And then they lived happily ever after', right? <br />And if there's anything Ben and Arthur are brilliant at, it's perfecting do-overs. So, fingers crossed!<br /><br />I loved every single character to pieces but none more so than Arthur. <br />Oh King Arturo!<br />The very instant that I saw you, (hmm not exactly) <br />did my heart fly to your service (totally). <br />Yeah, I KNOW he's gay and fictional, but he was just so adorable! 🙈<br /><br />Too many cute moments to count and some absolutely beautiful ones. And I loved every single one of it. <br />That awesome meet cute, kinda weird yet not creepy stalking, their dream like meet up, the perfect five first dates and an even better second date, Dylan's and Ben's bromance, summer school jokes, family dinners, subway rides, Broadway &amp; HP fanboying and everything else was unbelievably amazing. Even the fights, jealousies, insecurities and the other not so happy parts of Ben's and Art's relationship.<br /><br /><i> It should’ve been love at first sight like all the great stories, but I wasn’t ready yet. And that’s okay. We still got somewhere great. The worst story would’ve been never finding each other again, or ever meeting in the first place. </i><br /><br />*sobs*<br /><br />These two should have been endgame!!!!! <br />(yup, 6 exclamation points)</span>

<div id="review_2342868205" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2342868205" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2342868205?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062795243" href="/book/show/36260157-what-if-it-s-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=the-gay-agenda">the-gay-agenda</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=2018-faves">2018-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=heroes-i-adore">heroes-i-adore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=fluffy">fluffy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=hilarious">hilarious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=oh-my-god-marry-me">oh-my-god-marry-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2342868205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15958343829813526006"><b>--4.5 stars--</b><br/><br/>Massive thank you to Edelweiss and Harper Collins for sending me this ARC.<br/><br/>Can I just express how ecstatic I am at the state YA is headed this year? I've jokingly said that "20gayteen is in full swing and I am here for it" a lot, but in all seriousness, how amazing is it that YA is finally, FINALLY becoming more and more diverse with not only POC representation, but LGBTQ+ storylines being at the forefront. That's a big deal, people. It seems like only a few years ago YA was still, f</span>
  <span id="freeText15958343829813526006" style="display:none"><b>--4.5 stars--</b><br /><br />Massive thank you to Edelweiss and Harper Collins for sending me this ARC.<br /><br />Can I just express how ecstatic I am at the state YA is headed this year? I've jokingly said that "20gayteen is in full swing and I am here for it" a lot, but in all seriousness, how amazing is it that YA is finally, FINALLY becoming more and more diverse with not only POC representation, but LGBTQ+ storylines being at the forefront. That's a big deal, people. It seems like only a few years ago YA was still, for the most part, over-saturated with heteronormativity, so I'm glad that times are changing. Books like this one are part of the reason why I started getting back into reading this year.<br /><br />I think I speak for most of us when I say that this is a book that has been long-awaited; a gay YA novel told in that charming, traditional rom-com feel, set in New York City to boot. I was just so swept up in it immediately because it is an insanely adorable story. <br /><br />Arthur and Ben are such lovable characters in their own right, and their voices never blended due to how distinct they were from each other. Most of that is because of how different Becky Albertalli's and Adam Silvera's respective writing styles are. Albertalli's is more on the energetic and humorous side; I had so many laugh out loud moments in this book during Arthur's perspective. Silvera's writing is noticeably more laidback and understated by comparison. Both of their writing styles complimented each of the characters extremely well, gave them strong personalities unique from each other.<br /><br />The romance moved a little bit fast, I have to admit. I wouldn't say it was insta-love, no. Insta-love generally means romances that don't form naturally, they're just shoved in our faces from the get-go even though the characters clearly have a very contrived and forced connection. Arthur and Ben's romance was quite believable, I would say, so it didn't feel like insta-love to me. I would've liked if there was more time for them to truly connect, but I guess the fast pace was due to Arthur only staying in New York for the summer, so it's not like there's no reason for it.<br /><br />I have mixed feelings about the ending, though. Without spoiling any specific things, I appreciated the realism of it, but then I can't deny that I wanted extra cheese. This entire book was cheesy, but in a good way, and I wanted that to last up until the ending cause I like cheese once in a while, especially if's gay cheese. But still, I totally understood what the authors were going for with its open-endedness.<br /><br />This was simply a joy to read, though, honestly. Just such a fun summer romance set in the big city, very clearly inspired by classic rom-coms. I hope someday it gets adapted to the big screen as a mainstream Hollywood release, that would just be the homosexual cherry on top of this beautiful rainbow cake.<br /><br />Side note: Arthur in this book is a musical theater nerd and pure Hamiltrash, and like Ben, I'd never seen or heard the <i>Hamilton</i> soundtrack before. I guess I held back because I was bitter I would never get to actually see it live, but since this book has <i>Hamilton</i> written all over it, with a dash of <i>Dear Evan Hansen</i>, I think I'll finally cave and join bandwagon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15958343829813526006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2373449524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2373449524" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062795243" href="/book/show/36260157-what-if-it-s-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=good-covers">good-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2373449524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18291663009464586663">This review and other reviews can be found @ <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Thebookprescription</a><br/><br/><b>Actual Rating: 4.25 stars</b><br/><br/><i>I don’t know if we’re a love story or a story about love. But I know whatever we are that it’s great because we kept jumping the hoops in the first place.</i><br/><br/>🌟 This book is marshmallow and unicorns, this book is so cute! This is legitimately my favorite LGBT book till this point. I read 2 books by Adam and 1 book by Becky and enjoyed all of them but I had notes here and there, this was like the ultimate collab, </span>
  <span id="freeText18291663009464586663" style="display:none">This review and other reviews can be found @ <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Thebookprescription</a><br><br><b>Actual Rating: 4.25 stars</b><br><br><i>I don’t know if we’re a love story or a story about love. But I know whatever we are that it’s great because we kept jumping the hoops in the first place.</i><br><br>🌟 This book is marshmallow and unicorns, this book is so cute! This is legitimately my favorite LGBT book till this point. I read 2 books by Adam and 1 book by Becky and enjoyed all of them but I had notes here and there, this was like the ultimate collab, they just complete each other &lt;3.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497063410ra/22982722.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>🌟 To be honest, few pages into this and we have an insta-love scene that irked me, and then the characters explain themselves and I am convinced! And what is even better is that they don’t meet up until the end of the first third of the book! So the authors did not rush things, they made it as realistic as possible.<br><br>🌟 If I want to describe this book in short, I can say that it is an LGBT Heaven! I even learned some useful terminology in that regard! I have been following Adam on social media for a while and I could easily tell what he wrote (I know he loves to play Mario on Wii) &amp; what were his ideas, they both tried to make this as relevant as possible with many funny, modern &amp; relatable references!<br><br> <i> Happy Hudson loves boners but can never overcome flaccidity.</i><br><br>🌟 And I assure you by the end of this book you will be a better stalker! I mean the first part of the book had so many ideas for stalking that we all do in secret but they were chill with the whole topic, don’t get me wrong; this is not creepy stalking, this is more like real-life-crush-facebook-or-instagram stalking!<br><br>🌟 I feel like it is hard to talk about this without spoiling the good parts, but this is certainly the ultimate LGBT read of the year, and it is so gripping and easy to read that I didn’t even know when the whole thing finished. So, be sure to grab a copy when this is released!<br><br><br><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>

<div id="review_2148282576" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2148282576" />
    <a title="charlotte, (½ of readsrainbow)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow"><img alt="charlotte, (½ of readsrainbow)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587148844p2/7670260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2148282576?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="charlotte, (½ of readsrainbow)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="charlotte, (½ of readsrainbow)" href="/user/show/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow">charlotte, (½ of readsrainbow)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062795243" href="/book/show/36260157-what-if-it-s-us">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow?shelf=m-lgbt">m-lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow?shelf=disabilities-disorders-illnesses">disabilities-disorders-illnesses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow?shelf=lgbtq-authors">lgbtq-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow?shelf=latinx-characters">latinx-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow?shelf=ya-or-mg-lit">ya-or-mg-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7670260-charlotte-of-readsrainbow?shelf=f-lgbt-side">f-lgbt-side</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2148282576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4073340282291696046"><blockquote>
  <i>I don’t know if we’re in a love story or a story about love.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Review also posted on <a href='https://readsrainbow.wordpress.com/2018/10/02/arc-review-what-if-its-us/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reads Rainbow</a></i>
</b><br/><br/><b>Galley provided by publisher</b><br/><br/><b>Rep:</b> Puerto Rican mc, gay mcs, female bi side character<br/><br/>I did think that perhaps this was just one of those where I've grown out of the authors, but I actually reread <i>Simon vs the Homo Sapiens Agenda</i> earlier this year and still liked it just as much as the first time round, so it can't just be that. And this book did seem a whole lot more cringeworthy than any other b</span>
  <span id="freeText4073340282291696046" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I don’t know if we’re in a love story or a story about love.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Review also posted on <a href="https://readsrainbow.wordpress.com/2018/10/02/arc-review-what-if-its-us/" rel="nofollow noopener">Reads Rainbow</a></i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Galley provided by publisher</b><br /><br /><b>Rep:</b> Puerto Rican mc, gay mcs, female bi side character<br /><br />I did think that perhaps this was just one of those where I've grown out of the authors, but I actually reread <i>Simon vs the Homo Sapiens Agenda</i> earlier this year and still liked it just as much as the first time round, so it can't just be that. And this book did seem a whole lot more cringeworthy than any other books I've read by either author.<br /><br />To summarise the plot: Arthur meets Ben as he's getting rid of his ex-boyfriend's things at the post office. Unfortunately, before he can get a number, their meeting is interrupted by a lederhosen-clad flash mob (yeah, this was the first part where I went, <i>really?</i>). Anyway, that's the first 30 to 40 pages or so. The next 120 pages is dedicated to them... not meeting again. And then they do meet again. And follow that classic romance pattern.<br /><br />So, number one on my list of things I didn't really like about this book was the pacing. I don't need 120 pages of their day to day life before they meet again. And then I don't need another 150 pages of them dating (though seemingly, on Ben's part at least, while not actually wanting to date), before the inevitable and tedious (and overdramatic) breakup because of miscommunication. I feel like all this could have been condensed into a lot less than 450 pages. And so, because I have like, no patience, I got bored. Overall, though, I could have dealt with that, rated this book 2 stars maybe, but then came the kicker.<br /><br />It's overwhelmingly cringeworthy. Every other paragraph feels like it includes a pop culture reference (Hamilton and Harry Potter being common ones - and don't even get me started on that part where Arthur gets Ben to listen to the Hamilton soundtrack and then Ben makes a comment about <i>writing Hamilton/Harry Potter crossover fanfiction</i>. I physically recoiled from the computer). One or two I could deal with, but the sheer number of them in this? I was cringing at least once a chapter and that's really not fun. Not to mention the part where Arthur mistakes someone for Ansel Elgort and I had to feel the horror of a real life person being inserted into the narrative and subsequent secondhand embarrassment. It was not nice.<br /><br />A brief list of some other things that made me cringe along the way:<br /><br />&gt; "some kind of Kinsey scale Sorting Hat"<br /><br />&gt; when they talked about Pokemon fanfiction in real life<br /><br />&gt; when Arthur talks about the green M&amp;M being sexy along with some Looney Tunes characters on their first date<br /><br />&gt; and Harry Potter porn<br /><br />&gt; mentioning Draco/Hermione fanfiction<br /><br />But one particularly major cringe came from two points, both in Becky Albertalli's chapters. In one, Arthur and Ben are kissing when Arthur or Ben comments that maybe that's something Barack and Michelle (Obama) do on his birthday (why this comment? Because Barack Obama is Arthur's "forever president"?), and the other says more likely it's Obama and Justin Trudeau, <i>while Joe Biden watches</i>. Literally everything about this part is so creepy, starting with the fact that these are real people. But it does not stop here. Later on, a second joke is made along similar lines, but this time about porn between Mitch McConnell and Paul Ryan. Members of a party that wants to get rid of gay rights. Which, again these are <i>real people</i>, but this time it also just feeds back into the "all homophobes are secretly gay" line of argument. In the end, it was the cringeworthiness of the book that made me give it 1 star.<br /><br />One last point: I didn't actually much like Ben as a character either. He's honestly a bit of a dickhead, and spends his time when he's starting to date Arthur comparing him to his ex-boyfriend. And he writes a self-insert fantasy story, which is honestly, just another cringeworthy thing to add to the list. (Someone also pointed out to me that he's a bit like an Adam Silvera self-insert, and I am really scarred.)<br /><br />Maybe it'll be different for other readers, who don't find the pop culture references as cringey, and who are bigger fans of these authors, but in the end, it was just too much for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4073340282291696046" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ovAxd+4t+7nGrmnFesU6EZbn13oqwi1IwTaZOLVNuHC8HHlJM4iQ41kwd7C93VaHybUifciXeS0OSQryhe2Y3w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8YGA81foX02b7FeuXeBh0+hzxc6W44GJLo5+ksptCg3vbcjNik00FwRySdua+A1FtyEwyXS21ezh8e1Y+s0qog==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer7185614378990154734">Becky Albertalli is the author of the acclaimed novels Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda (film: Love, Simon), The Upside of Unrequited, and Leah on the Offbeat. She is also the co-author of What If It's Us with Adam Silvera. A former clinical psychologist who specialized in working with children and teens, Becky lives with her family in Atlanta. You can visit her online at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.beckyalbertalli.com'>www.beckyalbertalli.com</a>.</span>
